  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5a5c4b84-6bbc-4343-bef4-20c7ffee6edf'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16102734921343569218"><i>The Traitor</i> takes place two years after <i>The Son</i> and runs parallel with the early events in Divergent. In this robust story, readers follow Tobias as he uncovers the details of an Erudite plan that could threaten the faction system, and makes plans of his own to keep Abnegation safe. At the same time, Tobias is getting to know a new transfer initiate: Tris Prior.</span>

        });

<div id="review_2135834482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2135834482" />
    <a title="Ida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23173697-ida"><img alt="Ida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423853357p2/23173697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2135834482?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ida" href="/user/show/23173697-ida">Ida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23173697-ida?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2135834482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14614787142542569000"><b> Because this book runs parallel with the early events in "Divergent", minor spoilers may occur. </b><br/><br/><blockquote> <i> "How is it possible to live the same story twice, from different vantage points?" </i> </blockquote><br/><br/>This last Four story left me so conflicted, and I have no idea how to write this review. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504411319ra/23753310.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In this story, we follow Tobias as he struggles with the revelations from the previous stories, as well as some new information, while he´s getting to know Tris Prior. <br/>Strong, brave, iron-backboned Tris, who (at least in Divergen</span>
  <span id="freeText14614787142542569000" style="display:none"><b> Because this book runs parallel with the early events in "Divergent", minor spoilers may occur. </b><br><br><blockquote> <i> "How is it possible to live the same story twice, from different vantage points?" </i> </blockquote><br><br>This last Four story left me so conflicted, and I have no idea how to write this review. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504411319ra/23753310.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In this story, we follow Tobias as he struggles with the revelations from the previous stories, as well as some new information, while he´s getting to know Tris Prior. <br>Strong, brave, iron-backboned Tris, who (at least in Divergent) is one of my all-time-favorite heroines. <br><br><blockquote> <i> “Fear doesn’t shut you down,” I say. “It wakes you up. I’ve seen it. It’s fascinating.” Her eyes in every fear simulation, ice and steel and blue flame. The short, slight girl with the wire-taut arms. A walking contradiction. </i> </blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510575159ra/24431065.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To see their relationship evolve throughout this short story from Fours point of view was so much fun. <br><br><blockquote> <i> "Maybe she and I are the same."<br><br>"but openness is a habit you form over time, and not a switch you flip whenever you want to"<br><br>“See if you can figure out why they call me Four.” <br>The door closes behind us, and the room is black. She moves closer to me and says, “What’s your real name?” <br>“See if you can figure that out, too.”<br><br>"All I have to do is follow her, that’s all I have to do." </i>
</blockquote> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475080152ra/20678898.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And that kiss!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510575159ra/24431067.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At the start of this story, it seemed like Four was influenced by the opinions of others, and for a moment I wanted to slap him because it was so unlike the character we´ve seen before. But even if <b> we </b> know the right thing to do, his internal struggles are understandable, based on what he´s gone through. Warn Abnegation and betray your new faction. Don´t warn them, and betray his former faction. <br><br><blockquote> <i> "It wasn’t getting the tattoos that made me a faction traitor. It was what they meant to me—an escape from the narrow thinking of any one faction, the thinking that slices away at all the different parts of me, paring me down to just one version of myself."<br><br>"maybe I failed them when I chose Dauntless, and maybe I’m failing Dauntless now, but I don’t have to fail myself. And I, no matter what faction I’m in, know the right thing to do." </i> </blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510578436ra/24431383.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story is definitely a fitting conclusion to Fours short-stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14614787142542569000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3153984645" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3153984645" />
    <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis"><img alt="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585764390p2/6603759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3153984645?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis">☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3153984645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14006392447694711593">Q: I can’t be a pawn. But I’m not sure what I should be instead. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>She’s not learning the lessons Eric wants her to learn. She’s learning different things, wiser ones. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>Why do all dead people become heroes in Dauntless? Why do we need them to? Maybe they’re the only ones we can find in a faction of corrupt leaders, competitive peers, and cynical instructors. Dead people can be our heroes because they can’t disappoint us later; they only improve over time, as we forget more and more about </span>
  <span id="freeText14006392447694711593" style="display:none">Q: I can’t be a pawn. But I’m not sure what I should be instead. (c)<br />Q:<br />She’s not learning the lessons Eric wants her to learn. She’s learning different things, wiser ones. (c)<br />Q:<br />Why do all dead people become heroes in Dauntless? Why do we need them to? Maybe they’re the only ones we can find in a faction of corrupt leaders, competitive peers, and cynical instructors. Dead people can be our heroes because they can’t disappoint us later; they only improve over time, as we forget more and more about them. (c)<br />Q:<br />So if loyalty is impossible, what do I strive for instead? (c)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14006392447694711593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1109667777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109667777" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23733672-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459991403p2/23733672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109667777?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/23733672-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=why-do-girls-like-this-guy">why-do-girls-like-this-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=is-stupider-for-having-read-this">is-stupider-for-having-read-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=horrible-people">horrible-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=punch-a-protagonist">punch-a-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23733672-amanda?shelf=into-the-future">into-the-future</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109667777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17577712421494758288">What the hell is up with this series and it's obsession with Four and his four stupid fears?! It's like we can't go a single book or novella without taking a trip through it. It wasn't all that clever or entertaining the first time I read it what makes you think I'll like constant rehashing and copy pasting it into other works?<br/><br/>There is, once again, nothing new to see here folks. I had assumed that these were supposed to give deeper insight into this character, but they don't. Probably because th</span>
  <span id="freeText17577712421494758288" style="display:none">What the hell is up with this series and it's obsession with Four and his four stupid fears?! It's like we can't go a single book or novella without taking a trip through it. It wasn't all that clever or entertaining the first time I read it what makes you think I'll like constant rehashing and copy pasting it into other works?<br /><br />There is, once again, nothing new to see here folks. I had assumed that these were supposed to give deeper insight into this character, but they don't. Probably because there is no depth to him hence why the author has to keep beating in that he has four fears and his dad's an ass. <br /><br />The little tidbits we do learn just make him a bigger ass. Basically, he knew about major plot points during the original books but couldn't be assed to do anything about them. Just know that anything that was a dramatic reveal in the Divergent trilogy he already knew about. He knew that there was going to be an attack on the Abnegation but couldn't figure out what to do so just shrugged it off and eye humped Tris instead.<br /><br />Yeah, I can totally see why girls love this loser.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17577712421494758288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2066335774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6845971724403280044">uGH the last Four novella. I think I am kinda in love with Four now. <br/>I wouldn't say he is exactly my type when it comes to fictional book boyfriend. I am more likely to go crazy over the evil , diabolical, villain kind. <br/><br/>But there is so much to admire when it comes to Four. Four may appear as weak but he have this inner strength to him. At the same time, I can't help feeling sorry for him because he doesn't fit in Dauntless nor Abnegation and most of the time he is living in pretense. He have his</span>
  <span id="freeText6845971724403280044" style="display:none">uGH the last Four novella. I think I am kinda in love with Four now. <br />I wouldn't say he is exactly my type when it comes to fictional book boyfriend. I am more likely to go crazy over the evil , diabolical, villain kind. <br /><br />But there is so much to admire when it comes to Four. Four may appear as weak but he have this inner strength to him. At the same time, I can't help feeling sorry for him because he doesn't fit in Dauntless nor Abnegation and most of the time he is living in pretense. He have his hard times and he isn't as ruthless as a Dauntless should be but he still make it as the top initiate <br /><br />The Traitor shows how Four struggles being an initiate instructor. He is not as ruthless and as cruel as Eric. Four wanted a more peaceful and fair method when selecting the initiate but Eric wanted a competitive and tough method to select the initiate that basically ends in a lot of bloodshed. If you ask me its a hard choice to pick because Eric's method is more suited to the Dauntless motto, let nature run it course and weed out the weak ones while I don't see anything wrong in Four's preferred method. Plus the animosity Eric have toward Four only make Four's days harder. <br /><br />I find the romance between Four and Tris really forced. They are so boring together. <br /><br />I really want a novella from Eric's POV though and maybe even better Eric falls in love with Tris. Villains romance is hot</span>
  <a data-text-id="6845971724403280044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836914203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12395981872101091261">I'm not quite sure what to rate this one. Although I did enjoy it, I didn't on the same level as the others. Maybe it was just because it wasn't something completely new and unfamiliar since we know this part of the story, just from Tris' perspective. Having it from Four's is interesting and all, but it's not <i>quite</i> as unique as the other novellas about him. After reading all of these now, I've grown even fonder of his character, and I now want to go back and re-read <i>Divergent</i> and then see if I c</span>
  <span id="freeText12395981872101091261" style="display:none">I'm not quite sure what to rate this one. Although I did enjoy it, I didn't on the same level as the others. Maybe it was just because it wasn't something completely new and unfamiliar since we know this part of the story, just from Tris' perspective. Having it from Four's is interesting and all, but it's not <i>quite</i> as unique as the other novellas about him. After reading all of these now, I've grown even fonder of his character, and I now want to go back and re-read <i>Divergent</i> and then see if I can't finally push myself through <i>Insurgent</i>. That one just hasn't been able to grab me. I guess I'll go with a <b>3.5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12395981872101091261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1292562839" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1292562839" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13244359-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396758075p2/13244359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1292562839?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/13244359-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13244359-donna?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1292562839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4265681337072781014">I didn't like this novella as much. It was supposed to run parallel to the first part of book 1, Divergent. I didn't like the light that was centered on Four. It made him look weak and a little creepy and needy. That alone makes this seem contradictory to the first book in this series. But that wasn't the only thing that didn't ring true. There was so much more. So...2 stars. I was hoping for so much more. I think it is time to let the series rest. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1554079415" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1554079415" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1554079415?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"> ♥ Rebecca ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=extras">extras</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1554079415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10726950538202931102">This was the first of the short stories to catch up with the events from Divergent. It was interesting to see scenes we originally saw from Tris' POV from Four's, but I found it even more interesting to see what Four was up to behind the scenes. I did not realize how actively he was spying on his leaders and trying to stop the attack on Abnegation. I did not know that he knew so much about it in advance. There is a reason why this story is called The Traitor.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MF3o5PXQCfvQSmAAQ4J9xq8V1GaXjGJ0c1eIzBWM0c8oQ//QlUrmmlHovFaOghB4+APgp+66jpVugGU5ccbfhg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6OaRoWle/FR05v3dqXdrg1oCo03RoZ6HEBHXZgsh66rw+IaVCcQTNfVEIYtkdwY9DRSXjKiXcmYNxjqTb2vl4w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
